ملحق أول بالباب الثامن: مآخذ حول عوارض الأهلية
وأما أهلية الوجوب فكذلك متوافرة فيهما بطريق الأولوية لأن مناطها الصفة الإنسانية دون توقف على عقل أو سن.
وعدم إيجاب الصلاة على الحائض والنفساء وتأخير الصيام عنهما، لا يدل على معنى نقص الأهلية، بل معناه عدم توافر الشرائط الشرعية للتكليف، أو عدم انتفاء موانعه، بدليل أنَّ الصغير غير المميز لا تجب عليه الفرائض التعبدية ولا تصح منه بينما أنَّ أهلية الوجوب فيه كاملة منذ الولادة باتفاق الفقهاء كما تقدم، لأنَّ من شرائط إيجاب التكليف الشرعي البلوغ والعقل .
وقد قدمنا أنَّ الأهلية إنما تؤهل وتعد الشخص، ولكنها لا توجب لأن الإيجاب يتوقف على وجود سببه وتوافر شرائطه، وانتفاء موانعه (ر: ف ٤/٦٢) .
فعدم إيجاب الحكم الشرعي وعدم صحة الفعل لا يتعين أن يكونا ناشئين عن نقص في الأهلية، بل قد يكونان ناشئين عن فقدان بعض الشرائط الأخرى أو عن وجود بعض الموانع الشرعية كما هنا. وفرق عظيم بين فقدان الأهلية أو نقصها وبين انتفاء الشريطة أو وجود المانع ؛ وإلا أن تعتبر الجنابة أو النجاسة المانعة من صحة الصلاة عارضاً من عوارض الأهلية قياساً على الحيض الذي يمنع صحة الصوم ولا يسقطه، وهذا غير مقول ولا معقول.
وجب
والضابط في هذا التمييز أن ينظر إلى طبيعة العارض: فإذا كان له تأثير في ملكات الشخص العقلية وقابلياته كالجنون والعته والإغماء، أو تأثير في سلطته الشرعية يقتضي حماية الحقوق من تصرفاته، كالشفه، ومرض الموت وكالإفلاس في بعض الاجتهادات فعندئد يكون من عوارض الأهلية، وإلا فهو من الموانع أو من قبيل فقدان بعض الشرائط . قدمنا أول نظرية العقود بياناً كافياً للتعريف بالشرائط والموانع والأسباب والتمييز بينها فليرجع إليه ف ١/٢٨ - ٦) .
٨٥٥
Chapter Eight: The Theory of Legal Capacity and Guardianship
1 - Childhood is the natural prior stage of every human life; it is one of the original states in the subject of legal capacity and not among the temporary impediments. Some scholars of usul have objected to this objection and it was answered unconvincingly (see: Kashf al-Asrar 4/263).
2 - Forgetfulness is a normal condition that affects memory and is not an affliction that affects a person's body, mind, or legal status; it does not contradict legal capacity in any way nor diminish it. However, it is considered a legal excuse that removes accountability for neglecting some religious obligations or conditions, out of mercy for people and to remove hardship, as stated in the prophetic hadith: 'Indeed Allah has removed from my nation mistake, forgetfulness, and what they are coerced into.' (1) For example, one who forgets to pray in its time is not considered negligent; one who forgets to mention Allah's name over a slaughtered animal does not make it unlawful; one who eats in Ramadan forgetfully does not invalidate the fast.
3 and 4 - Menstruation and postnatal bleeding in women are legal preventers that prevent the obligation of some religious acts that require purity or prevent their practice. The menstruating woman and the woman with postnatal bleeding leave prayer and fasting, then make up the missed fasts of Ramadan but not the prayers; and they avoid entering mosques and reciting the Quran; and other exceptional rulings.
However, the capacity of obligation and the capacity of performance with their two branches (religious and civil) – i.e., capacity for worship and capacity for transaction – are complete in them.
- As for capacity of performance, its basis is intellect and awareness; hence it is established for the discerning minor within limited scope as previously mentioned. This intellect and awareness are fully present in the menstruating woman and the woman with postnatal bleeding, so menstruation and postnatal bleeding have no effect on their capacity of performance.
(1) See its source in vol. 2, p. 10b in the footnote.
854
-
First appendix to Chapter Eight: Objections regarding temporary impediments of legal capacity
As for capacity of obligation, it is likewise fully present in them by priority because its basis is human nature without dependence on intellect or age.
The non-obligation of prayer upon the menstruating woman and the woman with postnatal bleeding, and the postponement of fasting for them, does not indicate a deficiency in legal capacity. Rather, it means the absence of the legal conditions for obligation, or the non-removal of its preventers. This is evidenced by the fact that the non-discerning minor is not obligated with religious duties and they are not valid from him, yet his capacity of obligation is complete from birth by agreement of the jurists, as mentioned, because among the conditions for imposing legal obligation are puberty and intellect.
We have previously stated that legal capacity only qualifies and prepares a person, but it does not obligate, because obligation depends on the existence of its cause, fulfillment of its conditions, and absence of its preventers (see: vol. 4, p. 62b).
Thus, the non-imposition of a legal ruling and the invalidity of an act are not necessarily due to a deficiency in legal capacity; they may be due to the loss of some other conditions or the existence of some legal preventers as here. There is a great difference between loss or deficiency of legal capacity and the absence of a condition or existence of a preventer; otherwise, one would consider janabah (ritual impurity) or najasah (physical impurity) that prevent the validity of prayer as a temporary impediment of capacity by analogy to menstruation which prevents the validity of fasting without nullifying it, and this is neither said nor reasonable.
The controlling rule for this distinction is to look at the nature of the temporary impediment: if it affects a person's mental faculties and abilities like insanity, imbecility, and fainting, or it affects his legal authority necessitating protection of rights from his transactions, like safah (prodigality), death-illness, and insolvency in some juristic opinions, then it is among the temporary impediments of legal capacity. Otherwise, it is from the preventers or the category of loss of some conditions. We have previously presented at the beginning of the Theory of Contracts a sufficient explanation of the definition of conditions, preventers, and causes and the distinction between them, so refer to it (vol. 1, pp. 28-6).
855
Source pages p. 802

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) from the eighth chapter on legal capacity (ahliyyah) and its temporary impediments (’awāriḍ). The author, Dr. Muṣṭafā Aḥmad al-Zarqā, is explaining what qualifies as a true ’āriḍ (temporary impediment) affecting capacity as opposed to a mere preventer (māni‘) or lack of a condition (sharṭ).

The passage first clarifies that childhood (ṣighar) is an original state, not an ’āriḍ. Forgetfulness (nisyān) is a normal condition, not an impediment; it excuses but does not reduce capacity. Menstruation (ḥayḍ) and postnatal bleeding (nifās) are preventers that remove the obligation of certain acts (like prayer) but do not affect the underlying capacity: both capacity of obligation (ahliyyat al-wujūb) and capacity of performance (ahliyyat al-adā’) remain fully intact. The author emphasizes that non-obligation does not equal incapacity; it results from missing conditions (e.g., puberty) or existing preventers.

The key methodological rule (ḍābiṭ) is given at the end: an ’āriḍ is something that either (1) affects mental faculties (like insanity, imbecility, fainting) or (2) affects legal authority to protect others' rights (like prodigality, death-illness, insolvency in some views). Everything else is a preventer or loss of condition. This distinction is crucial for a mufti to correctly attribute rulings to the right cause.

Key Terms
عارض الأهلية (‘āriḍ al-ahliyyah): Temporary impediment affecting either mental faculties (like insanity) or legal authority (like safah), which diminishes or suspends capacity.
أهلية الوجوب (ahliyyat al-wujūb): Capacity to be subject to rights and obligations, rooted in human nature, present from birth.
أهلية الأداء (ahliyyat al-adā’): Capacity to perform valid legal acts, based on intellect and awareness.
المانع الشرعي (al-māni‘ al-shar‘ī): A legal preventer that removes obligation or validity of an act without affecting capacity itself, e.g., menstruation for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is classified as a true 'āriḍ (temporary impediment of legal capacity)?
A) Menstruation (ḥayḍ)
B) Forgetfulness (nisyān)
C) Imbecility (ʻatah)
D) Childhood (ṣighar)

Key Takeaway
A condition is a true temporary impediment of capacity only if it affects mental faculties or legal authority; otherwise it is a preventer or missing condition.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Distinguishing 'Awarid al-Ahliyyah from Other Obstacles
States a controlling rule for classifying capacity-affecting contingencies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi controlling rule (dabt) to classify any given contingent circumstance as either a true 'arid al-ahliyyah or an external impediment/condition, and justify your classification with reference to the nature of the effect.

Core Idea
A circumstance only affects capacity if it impairs mental faculties or legal authority; otherwise, it's a mere impediment or missing condition.

This lesson presents a crucial methodological tool (dabt) from Hanafi Rasm al-Mufti literature. The mufti must be able to distinguish between factors that truly impair legal capacity and those that simply prevent obligation or validity without affecting capacity. The passage provides a clear rule and applies it to four illustrative cases. Mastering this dabt is essential for accurate fatwa and legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Controlling Rule
Identify the two types of effects that qualify as 'arid al-ahliyyah: (1) impairment of mental faculties (e.g., insanity, imbecility, unconsciousness) and (2) impairment of legal authority requiring protection of rights (e.g., prodigality, terminal illness, bankruptcy in some views). Any other obstacle is either a legal impediment (mani') or a missing condition (shart).
The rule is a dabt, not a definitive enumeration; it guides analysis.
2
Apply to the Menstruation Counterexample
The passage uses menstruation to show that non-obligation of prayer does not imply deficient capacity. Analyze: menstruation does not affect mental faculties or legal authority; it simply creates a missing condition (ritual purity) for validity. Therefore, it is not an 'arid al-ahliyyah.
The same logic applies to post-natal bleeding and the example of a non-discerning minor.
3
Analyze Each Furu' (Branch Case)
For each of travel, ignorance, error, and jest, determine whether it satisfies the dabt. Travel: only creates hardship → concession (rukhsah), not capacity defect. Ignorance: excuse, not impairment. Error: negates intent, does not affect faculties. Jest: lacks true intention → invalidity due to deficiency in intent, not capacity. Note the exception for marriage, divorce, and manumission where jest is treated as serious.
Each furu' reinforces the distinction between capacity-affecting and non-capacity-affecting factors.
4
Evaluate the Exception for Jest
Jest normally invalidates contracts, but in marriage, divorce, and manumission, the Lawgiver treats it as serious despite the absence of true intent. This exception is based on specific textual evidence (hadith) and does not change the fact that jest does not affect capacity—it remains a matter of intention.
The exception is limited to these three areas; in all other contracts, jest leads to nullity.
5
Synthesize and Apply to a Novel Case
When encountering a new circumstance (e.g., intoxication, duress, coercion), apply the dabt: Does it affect mental faculties (reason, comprehension) or legal authority (capacity to manage property)? If yes, it is an 'arid al-ahliyyah; if no, look for impediments or missing conditions. This synthesis is the key skill for the mufti.
Always verify with the original sources and later fatwa compilations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ملحق أول بالباب الثامن: مآخذ حول عوارض الأهلية
وأما أهلية الوجوب فكذلك متوافرة فيهما بطريق الأولوية لأن مناطها الصفة الإنسانية دون توقف على عقل أو سن.
وعدم إيجاب الصلاة على الحائض والنفساء وتأخير الصيام عنهما، لا يدل على معنى نقص الأهلية، بل معناه عدم توافر الشرائط الشرعية للتكليف، أو عدم انتفاء موانعه، بدليل أنَّ الصغير غير المميز لا تجب عليه الفرائض التعبدية ولا تصح منه بينما أنَّ أهلية الوجوب فيه كاملة منذ الولادة باتفاق الفقهاء كما تقدم، لأنَّ من شرائط إيجاب التكليف الشرعي البلوغ والعقل .
وقد قدمنا أنَّ الأهلية إنما تؤهل وتعد الشخص، ولكنها لا توجب لأن الإيجاب يتوقف على وجود سببه وتوافر شرائطه، وانتفاء موانعه (ر: ف ٤/٦٢) .
فعدم إيجاب الحكم الشرعي وعدم صحة الفعل لا يتعين أن يكونا ناشئين عن نقص في الأهلية، بل قد يكونان ناشئين عن فقدان بعض الشرائط الأخرى أو عن وجود بعض الموانع الشرعية كما هنا. وفرق عظيم بين فقدان الأهلية أو نقصها وبين انتفاء الشريطة أو وجود المانع ؛ وإلا أن تعتبر الجنابة أو النجاسة المانعة من صحة الصلاة عارضاً من عوارض الأهلية قياساً على الحيض الذي يمنع صحة الصوم ولا يسقطه، وهذا غير مقول ولا معقول.
والضابط في هذا التمييز أن ينظر إلى طبيعة العارض: فإذا كان له تأثير في ملكات الشخص العقلية وقابلياته كالجنون والعته والإغماء، أو تأثير في سلطته الشرعية يقتضي حماية الحقوق من تصرفاته، كالشفه، ومرض الموت وكالإفلاس في بعض الاجتهادات فعندئذ يكون من عوارض الأهلية، وإلا فهو من الموانع أو من قبيل فقدان بعض الشرائط .

والسفر إنما اعتبر الشرع ما فيه من مشقة سبباً للترخيص في بعض الواجبات الدينية فبعض التكليفات جعله الشرع اختيارياً في حق المسافر، كصلاة الجمعة والعيدين والأضحية وبعضها سوغ للمسافر تأخيره عن وقته المعيَّن كصيام رمضان ..
فليس في السفر كما ترى مايخل بشيء من أهلية الشخص للوجوب أو للأداء من الناحية الدينية أو المدنية.
والجهل أيضاً لا يخل بشيء من أهلية الشخص وقابلياته، وإنما تنهض به للشخص في بعض المواطن معذرة شرعية مانعة من مؤاخذته على الإهمال، كمن أسلم وهو بعيد عن دار الإسلام جاهلاً للتكاليف التي يفرضها عليه الإسلام، فإن جهله في مثل هذه الحال يُعتبر عذراً مانعاً من مؤاخذته على إهمال الواجبات الدينية، وكجهل الوكيل بعزل موكله له، فإنَّ تصرفاته تبقى نافذة على الموكل حتى يبلغه خبر العزل. وفي هذه المسألة كما ترى كان العلم هو المسقط لسلطة الوكيل، والجهل مبقياً عليها؛ فليس في الجهل إخلال بالأهلية، وإنما هو معذرة.
والخطأ كذلك فقد عرفوه بأنه : وقوع الشيء على خلاف إرادة من وقع منه فليس فيه انتقاص من ملكات الشخص وقابلياته؛ ولا له بها أية صلة أو علاقة، وإنما هو وصف للأفعال الصادرة عن الشخص ينفي عنها القصد، الذي يوجد عادة في حالة التعمد فيقتضي رفع المؤاخذة أو تخفيفها.
وأبعد الكل عن معنى عوارض الأهلية الهزل!!
فالهزل ضد الجد، ومحله التصرفات القولية وهو تلاعب بالألفاظ دون قصد إلى معانيها وأحكامها ويترتب عليه عند الفقهاء بطلان العقود والتصرفات أو فسادها على خلاف تقدم في ذلك لانتفاء إرادة العاقد الحقيقة فيه لا لفقدان أهلية العاقد أو نقصانها بدليل أن الشارع اعتبر الهزل كالجد في بعض التصرفات استثناءاً، وهي النكاح والطلاق والإعتاق كما تقدم ر : ف (٦/٣٣)
First appendix to Chapter Eight: Considerations regarding contingencies of legal capacity.
As for capacity for obligation, it is likewise present in both (the man and the woman) by way of priority because its basis is the human attribute, without dependence on intellect or age.
The non-obligation of prayer upon the menstruating woman and the woman in post-natal bleeding, and the postponement of fasting for them, does not indicate a deficiency in capacity; rather its meaning is the non-existence of the legal conditions for obligation, or the non-removal of its impediments, as evidenced by the fact that the non-discerning minor is not obliged to perform devotional obligations nor are they valid from him, while capacity for obligation is complete in him since birth by agreement of the jurists, as previously mentioned, because from the conditions for rendering legal obligation obligatory are puberty and intellect.
We have already stated that capacity only qualifies and prepares the person, but it does not obligate, because obligation depends on the existence of its cause, the fulfillment of its conditions, and the absence of its impediments (see: F 4/62).
Thus, the non-obligation of a legal ruling and the invalidity of an act are not necessarily caused by a deficiency in capacity; rather they may be caused by the absence of some other conditions or the existence of some legal impediments, as here. And there is a great difference between the absence or deficiency of capacity and the non-fulfillment of a condition or the existence of an impediment; otherwise one would consider impurity or filth that prevents the validity of prayer as a contingency of capacity, by analogy to menstruation that prevents the validity of fasting but does not cancel it – and this is not said nor reasonable.
The controlling rule in this distinction is to look at the nature of the contingent circumstance: if it has an effect on the person's mental faculties and aptitudes, like insanity, imbecility, and unconsciousness, or an effect on his legal authority requiring protection of rights from his actions, like insanity (safah), terminal illness, and bankruptcy in some ijtihadat, then it is from the contingencies of capacity. Otherwise, it is from the impediments or from the category of absence of some conditions.

Travel: the Lawgiver considered the hardship therein as a cause for concession in some religious obligations; some obligations the Lawgiver made optional for the traveler, like Friday prayer, Eid prayers, and the sacrifice, and some he permitted the traveler to delay from its prescribed time, like the fast of Ramadan.
There is nothing in travel, as you see, that detracts from a person's capacity for obligation or performance, from a religious or civil perspective.
Ignorance also does not detract from a person's capacity or aptitudes; rather it arises for the person in some instances as a legal excuse preventing taking him to task for negligence, like one who becomes Muslim while far from dar al-Islam, ignorant of the obligations that Islam imposes upon him, for his ignorance in such a situation is considered an excuse preventing taking him to task for neglecting religious duties. And like the ignorance of an agent regarding his principal's dismissal: his actions remain binding on the principal until the news of dismissal reaches him. In this issue, as you see, knowledge is what removes the agent's authority, and ignorance preserves it. So there is no impairment of capacity in ignorance; it is merely an excuse.
Error likewise: they defined it as the occurrence of a thing contrary to the intention of the one from whom it occurs. There is no diminution of the person's faculties and aptitudes in it, nor does it have any connection or relation to them. Rather, it is a description of actions emanating from the person that negates from them the intent that usually exists in the case of deliberation, thus necessitating removal or mitigation of accountability.
And farthest of all from the meaning of contingencies of capacity is jest!
Jest is the opposite of seriousness, its locus is verbal actions, and it is playing with words without intending their meanings and legal effects. According to the jurists, it results in the nullity or invalidity of contracts and actions, with a difference previously mentioned, due to the absence of the true intention of the contracting party therein, not due to a loss or deficiency in the capacity of the contracting party, as evidenced by the fact that the Lawgiver considered jest like seriousness in some actions as an exception, namely marriage, divorce, and manumission, as previously mentioned: F 6/33.
Source pages p. 803

Commentary
This passage is a methodological appendix (Rasm al-Mufti) establishing a controlling rule (dabt) to distinguish between true 'awarid al-ahliyyah (contingencies affecting legal capacity) and other factors such as missing conditions (shurut) or legal impediments (mawani'). The author begins by affirming that capacity for obligation (ahliyyat al-wujub) is complete for all humans from birth, based on human nature, not on intellect or age. He then addresses potential counterexamples: menstruation and post-natal bleeding do not indicate deficient capacity; instead, they represent missing conditions for the obligation of prayer and fasting. The key evidence is that a non-discerning minor has full capacity for obligation yet is not obliged to perform devotional acts because conditions (puberty and intellect) are missing. The author emphasizes that capacity only qualifies a person; obligation requires a cause, conditions, and absence of impediments.
The controlling rule is then stated: examine the nature of the contingent circumstance. If it affects mental faculties (e.g., insanity, imbecility, unconsciousness) or legal authority (e.g., prodigality, terminal illness, bankruptcy in some views), it is a true 'arid al-ahliyyah. Otherwise, it falls under impediments or missing conditions.
The author applies this rule to four cases:
1. Travel (safar): The hardship of travel is a cause for concessions (rukhsah) like optional Friday prayer or delayed fasting, but it does not affect capacity. The traveler retains full capacity for obligation and performance.
2. Ignorance (jahl): Ignorance is an excuse preventing accountability for negligence. For example, a new Muslim in a non-Muslim land is not held liable for missed duties due to ignorance. Similarly, an agent's ignorance of his principal's dismissal preserves the agent's authority. Ignorance does not impair capacity.
3. Error (khata'): Error is defined as an action contrary to intention. It does not affect mental faculties; it only describes the act as unintentional, leading to reduced or removed liability. Capacity remains intact.
4. Jest (hazl): Jest is the opposite of seriousness, involving play with words without intending legal consequences. Jest leads to invalidity of contracts except in marriage, divorce, and manumission (where jest is treated as serious). The invalidity is due to lack of intention, not deficiency of capacity.
The passage reinforces that non-obligation or invalidity does not automatically imply deficient capacity. The mufti must carefully analyze the nature of the obstacle.

Key Terms
أهلية الوجوب (ahliyyat al-wujub): The capacity to have rights and obligations ascribed to a person, present from birth based on human nature.
عارض الأهلية ('arid al-ahliyyah): A contingency that affects mental faculties or legal authority, thus impacting capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada').
ضابط (dabt): A controlling rule that classifies contingencies as either 'awarid al-ahliyyah or otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the non-obligation of prayer upon a menstruating woman not considered a deficiency in her legal capacity?
A) Because menstruation is a form of insanity.
B) Because it indicates a missing condition for the obligation, not a capacity defect.
C) Because women have lesser capacity in Hanafi fiqh.
D) Because menstruation is a normal state and does not affect human nature.

Key Takeaway
A circumstance is an 'arid al-ahliyyah only if it directly impairs mental faculties or legal authority; otherwise, it is a mere impediment or missing condition.

Conditions for Considering Custom (al-Urf) - Four Essential Conditions
Listing and explaining the four conditions for custom to have legal authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for a custom to have legal authority and apply them to a hypothetical custom scenario.

Core Idea
A custom is authoritative only if it is consistent, present at the transaction, not contradicted by stipulation, and not conflicting with a text.

Custom (al-urf) is a recognized source of law in the Hanafi school, but it is not automatically binding. The fuqaha have laid down four precise conditions that must be satisfied. This lesson presents these conditions and explains their rationale, equipping the mufti to evaluate whether a given custom can be relied upon in legal decisions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions
List the four conditions from the passage. Each is a distinct requirement for a custom to be legally recognized.
Memorize these conditions as a checklist.
2
Distinguish consistency from prevalence
Understand that consistency (ittiraad) means the custom is followed in all cases; prevalence (ghalaba) means it is followed in most cases. Hanafis accept both, but consistency is stronger.
Example: dividing dowry into prompt and deferred is consistent if always done, prevalent if mostly done.
3
Apply the first condition to a custom
Use the dowry example from the text to see how the first condition works in practice.
4
Recognize the remaining three conditions
The second condition requires the custom to exist at the time of the transaction. The third forbids contradicting an explicit stipulation. The fourth forbids contradicting a definitive legal text.
These protect the parties' agreement and the primacy of shariah.
5
Evaluate a custom against all conditions
Given a hypothetical custom, check each condition in order. If any fails, the custom is not authoritative.
This is the mufti's real-world task.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل السبعون
شرائط اعتبار العرف

١/٧٠ - إنَّ ما تقدم بيانه من الاعتبار الشرعي للعرف، وماله من سلطان في ميدان الأحكام العملية بين الناس توليداً وتحديداً، مشروط بشرائط يجب توافرها في العرف لكي يكون له هذا السلطان. وتلك الشرائط التي يذكرها الفقهاء والأصوليون في مناسباتها المختلفة تتلخص بأربع:
1 أن يكون العرف مطرداً أو غالباً.
أن يكون العرف المراد تحكيمه في التصرفات قائماً عند إنشائها.
٣ - أن لا يعارض العرف تصريح بخلافه .
٤ - أن لا يعارض العرف نص شرعي بحيث يكون العمل بالعرف تعطيلاً له .
وسنتولى إيضاح هذه الشرائط فيما يلي:

٢/٧٠ - الشريطة الأولى أن يكون العرف مُطّرداً أو غالباً :
المراد هنا من اطراد العرف بين متعارفيه أن يكون عملهم به مستمراً في جميع الحوادث لا يتخلف. فالعرف مثلاً على تقسيم المهر في النكاح إلى معجل ومؤجل إنما يكون مطّرداً في البلد إذا كان أهله يجرون على هذا التقسيم في جميع حوادث النكاح.
والمراد من غلبة العرف أن يكون جريان أهله عليه حاصلاً في أكثر الحوادث.
Chapter Seventy: Conditions for Considering Custom. 1/70 - What has been previously explained of the legal consideration of custom, and the authority it has in the field of practical rulings among people, generating and determining, is conditional upon conditions that must be fulfilled in the custom for it to have this authority. These conditions, which the fuqaha and usuliyyun mention in their various contexts, are summarized in four: 1. That the custom be consistent or prevalent. 2. That the custom to be applied in transactions be existing at the time of their creation. 3. That the custom not contradict an explicit stipulation to the contrary. 4. That the custom not contradict a legal text such that acting upon the custom would nullify it. We will undertake to explain these conditions in what follows. 2/70 - The first condition: that the custom be consistent or prevalent. What is meant here by consistency of custom among those who practice it is that their practice of it be continuous in all cases, not omitted. For example, the custom of dividing the dowry in marriage into prompt and deferred is considered consistent in a town if its people follow this division in all marriage cases. And what is meant by prevalence of custom is that its practice by the people occurs in most cases.
Source pages p. 840

Commentary
This passage is a set of methodological rules for muftis. It outlines the four essential conditions for a custom to be legally recognized and authoritative. The conditions are: (1) the custom must be consistent (muttaarid) or at least prevalent (ghalib); (2) it must exist at the time of the transaction; (3) it must not contradict an explicit stipulation by the parties; (4) it must not contradict a definitive legal text (nass) such that following the custom would nullify that text. The author then elaborates the first condition, explaining that consistency means the custom is practiced in all instances without exception, while prevalence means it is practiced in the majority of cases. The example given is the custom of splitting the dowry into prompt and deferred portions: if the people of a town always do this, it is consistent; if they do it most of the time, it is prevalent. This condition ensures that the custom is a reliable indicator of common practice.

Key Terms
اطراد (ittiraad): Consistency: the custom is practiced continuously in all cases without exception.
غلبة (ghalaba): Prevalence: the custom is practiced in the majority of cases, even if not all.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first condition for a custom to be legally considered?
A) It must be ancient
B) It must be written down
C) It must be consistent or prevalent
D) It must be agreed upon by all scholars

Key Takeaway
Custom is authoritative only when it satisfies all four conditions: consistency/prevalence, existence at the time, non-contradiction with stipulation, and non-contradiction with a definitive text.

The First Condition for Custom: Ittirad or Ghalabah
Explains the first condition: custom must be continuous or predominant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition for valid custom and define ittirad and ghalabah with examples.

Core Idea
A custom must be practiced consistently or in most cases to have legal weight.

In this lesson, we examine the first condition a custom must satisfy before a mufti may rely on it. Custom is powerful, but not every habit qualifies. Must it be universal? Or is a predominant practice enough? Al-Zarqa clarifies the threshold.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
What is the first condition stated for valid custom? Locate it in the text.
2
Define ittirad
What does continuity (ittirad) mean? Use the example of mahr division.
It must be practiced in all events without exception.
3
Define ghalabah
What does predominance (ghalabah) mean? How does it differ?
It is practiced in most events, not necessarily all.
4
Understand the consequence
If a custom is practiced only half the time, what is it called and what is its legal status?
It is 'urf mushtarak and has no legal effect.

Source Text

الفصل السبعون
شرائط اعتبار العرف
١/٧٠ - إنَّ ما تقدم بيانه من الاعتبار الشرعي للعرف، وماله من سلطان في ميدان الأحكام العملية بين الناس توليداً وتحديداً، مشروط بشرائط يجب توافرها في العرف لكي يكون له هذا السلطان. وتلك الشرائط التي يذكرها الفقهاء والأصوليون في مناسباتها المختلفة تتلخص بأربع:
1 - أن يكون العرف مطرداً أو غالباً.
2 - أن يكون العرف المراد تحكيمه في التصرفات قائماً عند إنشائها.
3 - أن لا يعارض العرف تصريح بخلافه .
4 - أن لا يعارض العرف نص شرعي بحيث يكون العمل بالعرف تعطيلاً له .
وسنتولى إيضاح هذه الشرائط فيما يلي:

۲/۷۰ - الشريطة الأولى أن يكون العرف مُطّرداً أو غالباً :
المراد هنا من اطراد العرف بين متعارفيه أن يكون عملهم به مستمراً في جميع الحوادث لا يتخلف. فالعرف مثلاً على تقسيم المهر في النكاح إلى معجل ومؤجل إنما يكون مطّرداً في البلد إذا كان أهله يجرون على هذا التقسيم في جميع حوادث النكاح.
والمراد من غلبة العرف أن يكون جريان أهله عليه حاصلاً في أكثر الحوادث.

الباب التاسع : نظرية العرف
فاشتراط الاطراد أو الغلبة في العرف معناه اشتراط الأغلبية العملية فيه لأجل اعتباره حاكماً في الحوادث (۱)

فإنَّ العادة تسمى عرفاً متى اعتادها أكثر القوم ولو كانوا لا يجرون عليها إلا في أقل أعمالهم. وإذا تساوى عملهم بها وعدمه سميت عرفاً مشتركاً، وهو لا يعتبر في معاملات الناس ولا يصلح مستنداً ودليلاً للرجوع إليه في تحديد الحقوق والواجبات المطلقة، لأن عمل القوم به أحياناً إذا صلح دليلاً على قصدهم إلى تحكيمه فتركهم له أحياناً مماثلة أو أكثر ينقض هذه الدلالة .

ومن ثم كان من شرائط اعتبار العرف بنوعيه اللفظي والعملي، أن يكون مُطَّرداً أو غالباً بهذا المعنى.

والاطراد أو الغلبة لا يستلزمان أن يكون العرف عاماً، فإنَّ عموم العرف غير اطراده :
-
فالعرف العام هو الذي يكون منتشراً في جميع البلاد.
- والعرف الخاص هو الذي يتعارف في بلد أو بلدان معينة دون سواها، أو بين أهل حرفة أو صناعة مخصوصة دون سواهم، كما تقدم.
فكل من العرف العام والخاص يشترط لاعتباره وتحكيمه في المعاملات المطلقة أن يكون في محيطه مطرداً أو غالباً على أعمال أهله، لأنَّ العرف وإن كان عاماً، قد يكون غالباً في أعمال الناس بالمعنى المشروح أو لا يكون.

النصاب
(1) أما الأغلبية العددية بمعنى أن يكون العرف جارياً بين جميع القوم أو أكثرهم فهي ليست من قبيل الشرائط، بل هي ركن في تكوين العرف لا يتحقق معناه دونها؛ وهي التي تقدم بيانها لتحقق معنى العرف لأنّ العادة الفردية لا تصبح عرفاً إلا إذا اعتادها أكثر القوم في بيئتها، إذ العرف هو عادة الجمهور (ر: ف ١٠/٦٧ - ١١) ...
Chapter Seventy: Conditions for Considering Custom
1/70 - Indeed, what has been previously explained regarding the legal consideration of custom and its authority in the field of practical rulings among people, generating and specifying, is conditional upon conditions that must be fulfilled in the custom for it to have this authority. These conditions, which the jurists and usul scholars mention in their various contexts, are summarized in four:
1. That the custom be continuous or predominant.
2. That the custom intended to be applied in transactions exist at the time of their creation.
3. That the custom not contradict an explicit stipulation to the contrary.
4. That the custom not contradict a legal text such that acting on the custom would be a suspension of it.
We will clarify these conditions as follows:

2/70 - The first condition: that the custom be continuous or predominant:
What is meant here by continuity of custom among its practitioners is that their practice of it is continuous in all events without exception. For example, the custom of dividing the dowry in marriage into prompt and deferred is continuous in a town if its people follow this division in all marriage events.
What is meant by predominance of custom is that its practice by its people occurs in most events.

Chapter Nine: Theory of Custom
So the condition of continuity or predominance in custom means requiring practical prevalence in it for it to be considered governing in events (1).

For a habit is called a custom whenever most of the people adopt it, even if they only practice it in a minority of their actions. And if their practice of it and their omission are equal, it is called a shared custom, and it is not considered in people's transactions nor is it valid as a basis and evidence to refer to in determining absolute rights and obligations, because people's practice of it sometimes, if it serves as evidence of their intention to apply it, their abandonment of it at similar or more times negates this indication.

Hence, among the conditions for considering custom, both verbal and practical, is that it be continuous or predominant in this sense.

Continuity or predominance do not necessarily require that the custom be general, for generality of custom is different from its continuity:
- General custom is that which is widespread in all countries.
- Specific custom is that which is customary in a particular country or certain countries, or among people of a particular profession or industry, as previously mentioned.
So both general and specific custom require, for their consideration and application in absolute transactions, that within their scope they be continuous or predominant in the practices of their people, because a custom, even if general, may be predominant in people's practice in the explained sense or not.

Commentary:
(1) As for numerical majority, meaning that the custom is practiced by all or most of the people, that is not a condition, but rather a pillar in the formation of custom without which its meaning is not realized; it is what was previously explained for the realization of the meaning of custom, because an individual habit does not become a custom unless most of the people in its environment adopt it, for custom is the habit of the majority (see: p. 10/67-11)...
Source pages p. 840

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm explains the first condition for the validity of custom ('urf) as a source of law in the Hanafi madhhab. The author lists four conditions, and here details the first: the custom must be muttarid (continuous) or ghalib (predominant). Continuity means the custom is practiced in all relevant cases without exception; for example, the custom of dividing the mahr into mu'ajjal and mu'ajjal is continuous if everyone follows it in every marriage. Predominance means it is practiced in most cases, even if not all. The author then clarifies that this condition is about practical prevalence (al-aghlabiyya al-'amaliyya), not numerical majority. Numerical majority is actually a constitutive element (rukn) of custom, not a condition: a habit becomes a custom only when most people adopt it, but even then it must be consistently or predominantly practiced to be legally binding. If people practice it only half the time, it is a 'shared custom' (urf mushtarak) and carries no legal weight because the inconsistency negates any presumption of intent. The author also distinguishes between 'umum (generality) and ittirad (continuity): a custom may be general (across all lands) but still not be continuous in practice, so even general custom must meet the continuity/predominance condition to be valid in absolute transactions. This is a key rule for a mufti: when issuing fatwas based on custom, one must verify that the custom is actually and consistently applied in the relevant community, not merely known or theoretically accepted.

Key Terms
اطراد (ittirad): Continuity of custom meaning it is practiced in all events without exception.
غلبة (ghalabah): Predominance of custom meaning it is practiced in most events.
عرف مشترك (urf mushtarak): A custom practiced equally as often as abandoned; not legally binding.
عموم العرف (umum al-urf): Generality of custom meaning it is widespread across regions, distinct from continuity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best defines 'ittirad'?
A) Widespread across regions
B) Practiced in all relevant events
C) Practiced by most people
D) Not contradicted by a text

Key Takeaway
For a custom to be validly relied upon in fatwa, it must be consistently (muttarid) or predominantly (ghalib) practiced in the relevant community; mere generality or numerical majority is insufficient.

8 min
Distinguishing Continuity from Generality and the Status of Shared Custom
Clarifies that generality does not imply continuity, and defines 'urf mushtarak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between continuity/predominance of custom and its generality, and explain why 'urf mushtarak has no legal effect.

Core Idea
A custom can be general but still lack continuity; a shared custom is legally irrelevant.

Having learned that custom must be continuous or predominant, we now explore two common confusions: the difference between 'umum (generality) and ittirad (continuity), and the concept of 'urf mushtarak (shared custom). These distinctions are crucial for a mufti evaluating custom in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the distinction
State the difference between 'umum al-'urf and ittirad as given in the text.
'Umum is geographical spread; ittirad is consistency of practice.
2
Apply with an example
Give an example of a custom that is general (widespread) but not continuous.
Consider a practice followed in many countries but only in half the cases in each.
3
Define 'urf mushtarak
When is a custom called 'urf mushtarak and what is its ruling?
It is practiced and abandoned equally often; not binding.
4
Reason for the ruling
Why does a shared custom not count? Cite the text's reasoning.
Because inconsistent practice negates any presumption of intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل السبعون
شرائط اعتبار العرف
١/٧٠ - إنَّ ما تقدم بيانه من الاعتبار الشرعي للعرف، وماله من سلطان في ميدان الأحكام العملية بين الناس توليداً وتحديداً، مشروط بشرائط يجب توافرها في العرف لكي يكون له هذا السلطان. وتلك الشرائط التي يذكرها الفقهاء والأصوليون في مناسباتها المختلفة تتلخص بأربع:
1 - أن يكون العرف مطرداً أو غالباً.
2 - أن يكون العرف المراد تحكيمه في التصرفات قائماً عند إنشائها.
3 - أن لا يعارض العرف تصريح بخلافه .
4 - أن لا يعارض العرف نص شرعي بحيث يكون العمل بالعرف تعطيلاً له .
وسنتولى إيضاح هذه الشرائط فيما يلي:

۲/۷۰ - الشريطة الأولى أن يكون العرف مُطّرداً أو غالباً :
المراد هنا من اطراد العرف بين متعارفيه أن يكون عملهم به مستمراً في جميع الحوادث لا يتخلف. فالعرف مثلاً على تقسيم المهر في النكاح إلى معجل ومؤجل إنما يكون مطّرداً في البلد إذا كان أهله يجرون على هذا التقسيم في جميع حوادث النكاح.
والمراد من غلبة العرف أن يكون جريان أهله عليه حاصلاً في أكثر الحوادث.

الباب التاسع : نظرية العرف
فاشتراط الاطراد أو الغلبة في العرف معناه اشتراط الأغلبية العملية فيه لأجل اعتباره حاكماً في الحوادث (۱)

فإنَّ العادة تسمى عرفاً متى اعتادها أكثر القوم ولو كانوا لا يجرون عليها إلا في أقل أعمالهم. وإذا تساوى عملهم بها وعدمه سميت عرفاً مشتركاً، وهو لا يعتبر في معاملات الناس ولا يصلح مستنداً ودليلاً للرجوع إليه في تحديد الحقوق والواجبات المطلقة، لأن عمل القوم به أحياناً إذا صلح دليلاً على قصدهم إلى تحكيمه فتركهم له أحياناً مماثلة أو أكثر ينقض هذه الدلالة .

ومن ثم كان من شرائط اعتبار العرف بنوعيه اللفظي والعملي، أن يكون مُطَّرداً أو غالباً بهذا المعنى.

والاطراد أو الغلبة لا يستلزمان أن يكون العرف عاماً، فإنَّ عموم العرف غير اطراده :
-
فالعرف العام هو الذي يكون منتشراً في جميع البلاد.
- والعرف الخاص هو الذي يتعارف في بلد أو بلدان معينة دون سواها، أو بين أهل حرفة أو صناعة مخصوصة دون سواهم، كما تقدم.
فكل من العرف العام والخاص يشترط لاعتباره وتحكيمه في المعاملات المطلقة أن يكون في محيطه مطرداً أو غالباً على أعمال أهله، لأنَّ العرف وإن كان عاماً، قد يكون غالباً في أعمال الناس بالمعنى المشروح أو لا يكون.

النصاب
(1) أما الأغلبية العددية بمعنى أن يكون العرف جارياً بين جميع القوم أو أكثرهم فهي ليست من قبيل الشرائط، بل هي ركن في تكوين العرف لا يتحقق معناه دونها؛ وهي التي تقدم بيانها لتحقق معنى العرف لأنّ العادة الفردية لا تصبح عرفاً إلا إذا اعتادها أكثر القوم في بيئتها، إذ العرف هو عادة الجمهور (ر: ف ١٠/٦٧ - ١١) ...
Chapter Seventy: Conditions for Considering Custom
1/70 - Indeed, what has been previously explained regarding the legal consideration of custom and its authority in the field of practical rulings among people, generating and specifying, is conditional upon conditions that must be fulfilled in the custom for it to have this authority. These conditions, which the jurists and usul scholars mention in their various contexts, are summarized in four:
1. That the custom be continuous or predominant.
2. That the custom intended to be applied in transactions exist at the time of their creation.
3. That the custom not contradict an explicit stipulation to the contrary.
4. That the custom not contradict a legal text such that acting on the custom would be a suspension of it.
We will clarify these conditions as follows:

2/70 - The first condition: that the custom be continuous or predominant:
What is meant here by continuity of custom among its practitioners is that their practice of it is continuous in all events without exception. For example, the custom of dividing the dowry in marriage into prompt and deferred is continuous in a town if its people follow this division in all marriage events.
What is meant by predominance of custom is that its practice by its people occurs in most events.

Chapter Nine: Theory of Custom
So the condition of continuity or predominance in custom means requiring practical prevalence in it for it to be considered governing in events (1).

For a habit is called a custom whenever most of the people adopt it, even if they only practice it in a minority of their actions. And if their practice of it and their omission are equal, it is called a shared custom, and it is not considered in people's transactions nor is it valid as a basis and evidence to refer to in determining absolute rights and obligations, because people's practice of it sometimes, if it serves as evidence of their intention to apply it, their abandonment of it at similar or more times negates this indication.

Hence, among the conditions for considering custom, both verbal and practical, is that it be continuous or predominant in this sense.

Continuity or predominance do not necessarily require that the custom be general, for generality of custom is different from its continuity:
- General custom is that which is widespread in all countries.
- Specific custom is that which is customary in a particular country or certain countries, or among people of a particular profession or industry, as previously mentioned.
So both general and specific custom require, for their consideration and application in absolute transactions, that within their scope they be continuous or predominant in the practices of their people, because a custom, even if general, may be predominant in people's practice in the explained sense or not.

Commentary:
(1) As for numerical majority, meaning that the custom is practiced by all or most of the people, that is not a condition, but rather a pillar in the formation of custom without which its meaning is not realized; it is what was previously explained for the realization of the meaning of custom, because an individual habit does not become a custom unless most of the people in its environment adopt it, for custom is the habit of the majority (see: p. 10/67-11)...
Source pages p. 840

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm explains the first condition for the validity of custom ('urf) as a source of law in the Hanafi madhhab. The author lists four conditions, and here details the first: the custom must be muttarid (continuous) or ghalib (predominant). Continuity means the custom is practiced in all relevant cases without exception; for example, the custom of dividing the mahr into mu'ajjal and mu'ajjal is continuous if everyone follows it in every marriage. Predominance means it is practiced in most cases, even if not all. The author then clarifies that this condition is about practical prevalence (al-aghlabiyya al-'amaliyya), not numerical majority. Numerical majority is actually a constitutive element (rukn) of custom, not a condition: a habit becomes a custom only when most people adopt it, but even then it must be consistently or predominantly practiced to be legally binding. If people practice it only half the time, it is a 'shared custom' (urf mushtarak) and carries no legal weight because the inconsistency negates any presumption of intent. The author also distinguishes between 'umum (generality) and ittirad (continuity): a custom may be general (across all lands) but still not be continuous in practice, so even general custom must meet the continuity/predominance condition to be valid in absolute transactions. This is a key rule for a mufti: when issuing fatwas based on custom, one must verify that the custom is actually and consistently applied in the relevant community, not merely known or theoretically accepted.

Key Terms
اطراد (ittirad): Continuity of custom meaning it is practiced in all events without exception.
غلبة (ghalabah): Predominance of custom meaning it is practiced in most events, even if not all.
عرف مشترك (urf mushtarak): A custom practiced equally as often as abandoned; not legally binding.
عموم العرف (umum al-urf): Generality of custom meaning it is widespread across regions, distinct from continuity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is an 'urf mushtarak?
A) A custom practiced everywhere
B) A custom practiced half the time
C) A custom that contradicts a text
D) A custom practiced by a minority

Key Takeaway
Continuity/predominance is distinct from generality; a shared custom (practiced as often as not) has no legal weight.

Third Condition: Custom Must Not Conflict with Explicit Stipulation
Explaining the third condition and its exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the third condition for the validity of custom, explain the maxim 'la ibra lil-dalalah fi muqabil al-tasrih', and apply the condition to cases in ijarah and ariyah.

Core Idea
Explicit stipulation overrides custom; custom only governs when parties are silent.

This passage introduces the third condition for custom to be legally binding: it must not contradict an explicit stipulation. The reason is that custom operates as an implied condition (dalalah), which is subordinated to explicit statements. You will learn the governing maxim and its application in hire and loan contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the condition and its rationale
Read the opening sentence of the passage. Identify the condition: custom must not contradict an explicit stipulation. Understand that custom is only relevant when parties are silent; their explicit words take precedence.
Memorize the maxim: 'لا عبرة للدلالة في مقابلة التصريح'.
2
Analyze the examples from Ijarah and Ariyah
Review the examples from hire (ijarah) and loan (ariyah). Note how in each case the explicit stipulation overrides the custom, and identify the consequence (e.g., borrower becomes usurper if he exceeds restrictions).
3
Identify the exception for impossible stipulations
The passage notes that if the explicit stipulation is impossible to fulfill (e.g., working without sleep for a month), the contract is invalid due to gharar. Understand that this is an exception to the general rule that explicit stipulations are binding.
This exception is governed by the maxim 'الغرر المنفي في العقود'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤/٧٠ - الشريطة الثالثة : أن لا يعارض العرف تصريح بخلافه : هذه الشريطة قيد أساسي في القاعدة المتقدمة في بيان عرف المعاملات، وهي أن المعروف عرفاً كالمشروط شرطاً». فقد تقدم أن علة تنزيل الأمر المعروف منزلة المشروط هي سكوت المتعاقدين عن الأمر المتعارف وعدم اشتراطهم إياه صراحة اعتماداً على العرف الجاري. فإثبات الحكم المتعارف في هذه الحال إنما هو من قبيل الدلالة، فإذا صرح بخلافه بطلت هذه الدلالة، إذ من القواعد الفقهية المقررة أنه: «لا عبرة للدلالة في مقابلة التصريح». يقول الإمام عز الدين عبد العزيز بن عبد السلام الشافعي في كتابه «قواعد الأحكام» (١٧٨/٢): كل ما يثبت بالعرف إذا صَرَّح المتعاقدان بخلافه بما يوافق مقصود العقد، ويمكن الوفاء به صح. فلو شرط المستأجر على الأجير أن يستوعب النهار بالعمل من غير أكل وشرب ويقطع المنفعة لزمه ذلك. ولو شرط عليه أن يعمل شهراً في الليل والنهار بحيث لا ينام ليلاً ولا نهاراً فالذي أراه بطلان هذه الإجارة لتعذر الوفاء به فكان ذلك غرراً لا تمس الحاجة إليه. ويقول العلامة التركي علي حيدر في شرح المادة ٣٧ من المجلة : إنَّ العرف يكون حجة إذا لم يكن مخالفاً لنص أو شرط لأحد العاقدين. فلو استأجر شخص أجيراً للعمل من الظهر إلى العصر فقط ليس له أن يلزمه بالعمل من الصباح إلى المساء بحجة أن عرف البلدة هكذا. وعلى ذلك تتقيد الإعارة في الزمان والمكان والمقدار بما يقيدها المعير ولو جاء قيده مخالفاً للمعتاد، إذ لا عبرة للمعتاد مع التصريح بخلافه. فلو استعار شخص دابة مثلاً للركب أو للتحميل يعتبر مأذوناً بركوبها أو بتحميلها القدر المعتاد في أمثالها عرفاً. ولكن لو نهاه المعير صراحة عن ركوبها أكثر من مدة أو عن تحميلها أكثر من مقدار حددهما له، لا يجوز للمستعير أن يزيد عليه ولو مقداراً لا يتجاوز المعتاد. فإن زاد كان متعدياً في حكم الغاصب.
4/70 - The third condition: That custom does not contradict an explicit stipulation to the contrary. This condition is a fundamental restriction in the aforementioned rule concerning the custom of transactions, namely that 'what is known by custom is like what is stipulated as a condition.' It has been previously mentioned that the reason for treating the customary matter as if it were stipulated is the silence of the contracting parties regarding the customary matter and their failure to stipulate it explicitly, relying on the prevailing custom. Thus, establishing the customary ruling in this case is by way of implication. If the contrary is explicitly stated, this implication becomes void, because one of the established legal maxims is: 'No regard is given to implication in the face of explicit statement.' Imam 'Izz al-Din 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn 'Abd al-Salam al-Shafi'i says in his book Qawa'id al-Ahkam (2/178): Everything established by custom, if the contracting parties explicitly state the opposite in a manner consistent with the purpose of the contract and capable of fulfillment, it is valid. For example, if the lessee stipulates on the worker that he must work the entire day without eating or drinking and interrupts the benefit, it is binding on him. But if he stipulates that he work a month day and night without sleeping at all, what I see is the invalidity of this hire because it is impossible to fulfill, so it is a gharar (uncertainty) for which there is no need. The Turkish scholar 'Ali Haydar says in his commentary on Article 37 of the Majalla: Custom is authoritative only if it does not conflict with a text or a stipulation of one of the contracting parties. So if a person hires a worker to work from noon to afternoon only, he cannot compel him to work from morning to evening under the pretext that the custom of the town is such. Similarly, a loan is restricted in time, place, and quantity by what the lender restricts, even if the restriction contradicts the customary, because there is no regard for custom when the contrary is explicitly stated. For instance, if a person borrows an animal for riding or for loading, he is considered authorized to ride or load it to the customary extent. But if the lender explicitly forbids him from riding it beyond a certain period or from loading it beyond a certain amount specified to him, the borrower may not exceed that, even by an amount not exceeding the customary. If he exceeds, he is a transgressor subject to the ruling of a usurper.
Source pages p. 844

Commentary
This passage presents the third condition for the validity of custom (al-'urf) in legal transactions. The author begins by stating the condition: custom must not contradict an explicit stipulation to the contrary. He links this to the fundamental rule that 'what is known by custom is like what is stipulated as a condition' (al-ma'ruf 'urfan ka al-mashrut shartan). The rationale is that the customary ruling operates only when the parties are silent; their explicit agreement overrides the custom. The author then quotes Imam 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam (Shafi'i) and 'Ali Haydar (Hanafi) to illustrate the point. Examples are given from hire (ijarah) and loan (ariyah). For instance, a hire contract specifying working hours from noon to afternoon prevents the employer from demanding work from morning to evening based on custom. Similarly, a lender's explicit restriction on time or quantity of use takes precedence over customary usage. If the borrower exceeds such restrictions, he becomes a usurper (ghasib). This condition is essential: explicit stipulations always override custom, provided they are possible and consistent with the contract's purpose. Impossible stipulations (like working without sleep for a month) render the contract invalid due to gharar (excessive uncertainty).

Key Terms
العرف (al-'urf): Customary practice prevalent among people in transactions or speech
التصريح (al-tasrih): Explicit stipulation or statement by a contracting party
الدلالة (al-dilalah): Implication or indication from silence or custom

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule explained in this passage, if a lender explicitly restricts the borrower to riding the animal for one hour, but the customary usage in the town is to allow riding for two hours, what is the ruling?
A) The borrower may ride for two hours because custom overrides the restriction.
B) The borrower must ride only for one hour; if he rides more, he becomes a usurper.
C) The contract is void because the restriction contradicts custom.
D) The borrower must seek permission from the lender each time.

Key Takeaway
Explicit stipulations always prevail over custom; custom only operates in silence.

When Custom Collides with a Specific Text
Defining the rule that a specific textual prohibition nullifies contradictory custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a custom conflicts with a specific textual prohibition and apply the rule that the text must prevail, including recognizing the exceptional case of necessity.

Core Idea
Custom cannot override a specific text; the text must be implemented.

Custom ('urf) is a recognized source in Hanafi fiqh, but its authority is not absolute. When a custom directly contradicts a specific prohibition from the Qur'an or Sunnah (nass khas), that custom is null and void. This lesson explains the rule, its rationale, and its applications, drawing on examples from the Sharia and analogies from modern legal systems.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict
Recognize the situation: a custom is practiced by the people, and there is a specific textual prohibition from the Lawgiver on that exact matter. Determine if the custom challenges the text.
The custom may be general or specific, pre-existing or emerging after the text.
2
Apply the rule of text over custom
The custom is invalid and must be abandoned. The text is binding and cannot be suspended by contrary practice, except in genuine emergencies where the Lawgiver Himself allows temporary dispensation.
3
Examine the rationale
The Sharia is legislated to guide people toward the common good. The Lawgiver's assessment of harm overrides any perceived benefit from the custom. Disregarding the text undermines the very purpose of legislation.
Refer to al-Shatibi's al-Muwafaqat for deeper maqasid reasoning.
4
Review the applied examples
Study the pre-Islamic customs that were prohibited: adoption (tabanni), internal raids (ghazw), and contracts with gharar (munabadha, mulamasa, etc.). These illustrate how the rule operates in different chapters of fiqh.
These examples are from the source text; they are not exhaustive.
5
Distinguish the exception of necessity
Necessity (idtrar) can temporarily override the text, but only as permitted by the Lawgiver. This is governed by the maxim 'al-darurat tubih al-mahzurat' (necessities permit the prohibited).
The exception does not validate the custom as a permanent ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل (۷۱) اصطدام العرف بنص تشريعي خاص
وسنرى تفصيل هذه الحالات في الفصول التالية:
حالة اصطدام العرف بنص تشريعي خاص
۳/۷۱ - إذا تعارف الناس على عمل من الأعمال العادية أو المدنية، وكان الأمر الذي تعارفوه منهياً عنه وممنوعاً بنص خاص، أي بنص وارد عن الشارع لمنع هذا الأمر بخصوصه، كما كان الجاهليون متعارفين التبني مثلاً وإجراء حكم البنوة الحقيقة فيه، فنهى عنه القرآن بخصوصه، فإن هذا العرف عندئذ لا اعتبار له ولا قيمة. فهو عرف مرفوض يجب تغييره لا إقراره، ولا يجوز القضاء به بحال سواء أكان العرف خاصاً أو عاماً، وسواء أكان حادثاً بعد ورود النص، أو قائماً قبله.
وذلك لأنه لما صادم العرف إرادة الشارع الخاصة في موضوع ما أصبح الفقيه المكلف بتطبيق الشرع بين أمرين اثنين:
إما أن يعمل بالعرف وهذا إهمال تام لنص الشارع، وذلك لا يسوغ إلا في أحوال الاضطرار الطارىء، لأنّ الشارع نفسه قد شَرَع الإهمال الموقت في الأحوال الاضطرارية.
وإما أن يعمل بالنص ويهمل العرف وهذا الذي يجب المصير إليه.
فمن البديهي أن الشريعة إلزامية ولم تشرع إلا لكي تنفذ نصوصها وتحترم. فلا يجوز تعطيلها بالتعامل على خلافها وإلا لم يبق للتشريع معنى (ر: «الموافقات للشاطبي المسألة / ١٤/ من النوع الرابع من كتاب المقاصد /٢٨٣/٢ - ٢٨٤).
٤/٧١ - وقد أسلفنا أن من الأعراف ما يكون في ذاته حسناً عادلاً، ومنها ما يكون قبيحاً وجائراً، وإن من مقاصد الشرائع التي تسن أن تقرّ الحسن وتنهى عن القبيح، وتوجّه الناس في أعمالهم ومعاملاتهم إلى الخير العام. والمرجع في تمييز الحسن العادل من القبيح الجائر إنما هو أمر الشارع ونهيه لأنَّ الشارع يزن الأمور وينظر إلى نتائجها من جميع نواحيها من بعض النواحي دون بعض. فما نهى عنه بخصوصه يجب أن يُعتبر مضراً ولو أنه نافع لمئات أو فئات (ر: ف٧/٦٧).
وكل تشريع إنما يقوم على أساس تقييد حرية المكلفين في بعض ميادين العمل وإطلاقها في بعض، بحسب ما يرى الشارع ويقدر من وجوه المصلحة العامة. وقد تتفاوت حدود هذا الإطلاق والتقييد بين شريعة وأخرى. وهذا مقرَّر في النظريات القانونية اليوم أيضاً، فنصوص القوانين لا يغير حكمها العرف المخالف.
ونظير هذا نظر القوانين الوضعية اليوم إلى قضايا وأحكام يراها واضع القانون من النظام العام فيحجر حرية المكلفين عن كل اتفاق أو عرف على خلافها، ويعتبره باطلا (۱).
٥/٧١ - ولذا جاءت الشريعة الإسلامية بالنهي عن كثير من الأعمال والعقود التي كانت متعارفة في الجاهلية بلا نكير فحرمت الغزو الداخلي واستباحة الناس الأموال والأعراض به وأقامت دولة ونظاماً أخلاقياً واجتماعياً وحقوقياً أخضعت له الجميع، مع أن الغزو الداخلي كان عرفاً مألوفاً في جاهلية العرب ولا يزال معتاداً لدى قبائل من البدو في بوادي بلادنا وغيرها.
وكذلك نهى النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن عقود كانت متعارفة بين العرب لانتفاء التراضي الحر فيها لما فيها من غرر ومشكلات. من نهيه عن البيع بالمنابذة والملامسة وإلقاء الحجر، وبيع الملاقيح والمضامين (۱).
Chapter 71: Collision of Custom with a Specific Legislative Text. We will see the details of these cases in the following chapters: Case of collision of custom with a specific legislative text. 3/71 - If people customarily engage in an ordinary or civil practice, and that practice is prohibited and forbidden by a specific text, i.e., a text from the Lawgiver specifically prohibiting this matter, as for example the pre-Islamic Arabs customarily practiced adoption and applied the ruling of true sonship therein, and the Qur'an specifically prohibited it, then this custom has no consideration or value. It is a rejected custom that must be changed, not affirmed, and it is not permissible to judge by it in any case, whether the custom is specific or general, and whether it arose after the text or existed before it. That is because when custom conflicts with the specific will of the Lawgiver in a subject, the jurist tasked with applying the Sharia is faced with two options: Either to act by the custom, which is a complete disregard for the text of the Lawgiver, and this is not permissible except in cases of sudden necessity, because the Lawgiver Himself has legislated temporary disregard in emergency situations. Or to act by the text and disregard the custom, and this is what must be followed. It is obvious that the Sharia is binding and was only legislated so that its texts be implemented and respected. It is not permissible to suspend it by acting contrary to it, otherwise legislation would have no meaning. (Ref: al-Muwafaqat by al-Shatibi, issue 14, type 4 of the Book of Maqasid, 2/283-284). 4/71 - We have already mentioned that some customs are in themselves good and just, and some are ugly and unjust. And indeed one of the objectives of legislated laws is to affirm the good and prohibit the ugly, and to guide people in their actions and transactions toward the common good. The reference in distinguishing good and just from ugly and unjust is only the command and prohibition of the Lawgiver, because the Lawgiver weighs matters and looks at their consequences from all aspects, not from some aspects alone. Whatever He specifically prohibited must be considered harmful, even if it benefits hundreds or groups. (Ref: f/7/67). And every legislation is based on restricting the freedom of the obligated persons in some fields of action and releasing it in others, according to what the Lawgiver sees and estimates of public interest. The limits of this restriction and release may vary between one legal system and another. This is also established in modern legal theories: the rulings of laws are not changed by contrary custom. Analogous to this is the view of positive laws today regarding issues and rulings that the legislator considers to be of public order, so he restricts the freedom of the obligated persons from any agreement or custom contrary to them, and considers it void. 5/71 - And thus Islamic Sharia came with the prohibition of many practices and contracts that were customary in pre-Islamic times without denial. It prohibited internal raids and the plundering of people's wealth and honor thereby, and established a state and an ethical, social, and legal system to which everyone submitted, even though internal raids were a familiar custom in pre-Islamic Arab society and are still practiced among Bedouin tribes in the deserts of our country and others. Likewise, the Prophet ﷺ prohibited contracts that were customary among the Arabs because of the lack of free consent therein due to gharar and problems. Among his prohibitions: the sale by munabadha, mulamasa, throwing the stone, and the sale of al-malaqih and al-madamin.
Source pages p. 848

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule in usul al-iftaa: when a custom ('urf) clashes with a specific textual prohibition (nass khas), the custom is invalid and must be abandoned. The author, Mustafa al-Zarqa, clarifies that this applies whether the custom arose before or after the text, and whether it is general or specific. He supports this with examples from the Sharia: the prohibition of adoption (tabanni), which was a pre-Islamic custom, and the prohibition of various pre-Islamic contracts involving uncertainty (gharar). He also likens this to modern positive law, where mandatory rules of public order cannot be overridden by contrary custom. The rule is based on the binding nature of Sharia and the fact that the Lawgiver's assessment of harm overrides any perceived benefit. The passage emphasizes that the mufti must prioritize the text over custom, except in genuine emergencies where temporary dispensation is allowed by the Lawgiver Himself.

Key Terms
العرف (al-urf): A practice that people customarily follow in their dealings, whether good or bad.
النص الخاص (al-nass al-khas): A specific textual prohibition from the Lawgiver (Qur'an or Sunnah) regarding a particular matter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a custom that existed before a specific divine prohibition?
A) The custom is valid because it predates the text.
B) The custom is invalid and must be abandoned.
C) The custom is valid only if it is general.
D) The custom is valid but can be gradually phased out.

Key Takeaway
A specific textual prohibition overrides any contrary custom, regardless of how widespread or longstanding that custom is, except in genuine emergencies where temporary dispensation is allowed.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Custom Cannot Override an Explicit Legal Text
Explaining the principle that explicit legal texts override contradictory customs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'No consideration is given to a custom that contradicts a legal text' to identify when a custom is invalid and explain the Hanafi rationale.

Core Idea
Custom cannot override an explicit Quranic or Prophetic text – the Lawgiver's prohibition overrides any widespread practice.

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental principle in Hanafi legal theory: custom (al-ʿurf) is a recognized source of law, but it is subordinate to explicit texts (nusus). Dr. Mustafa al-Zarqa explains that the Lawgiver's specific prohibitions take precedence over any contrary custom, no matter how widespread. Using examples from pre-Islamic practices that Islam abolished, the passage demonstrates that even if a prohibited practice re-emerges and becomes customary, it remains legally invalid. This lesson is essential for muftis and students of iftaa to understand the hierarchy of legal sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim
State the principle that custom cannot override a legal text. The maxim is: 'لا عبرة لعرف يخالف نصاً شرعياً' (No consideration is given to a custom that contradicts a legal text).
This is a intermediate-level maxim (wusta).
2
Understand the Lawgiver's authority
Recognize that the Lawgiver (Allah) evaluates actions holistically; specific prohibitions indicate harm. The passage emphasizes that what Allah prohibits is harmful even if it appears beneficial to many.
This ties to the wisdom behind legislation.
3
Explore the examples
Work through the examples given: shighar marriage, debtor enslavement, invalid sales (munabadhah, mulamasah, etc.). Note how each was a pre-Islamic custom that Islam explicitly prohibited.
The examples show that even widespread acceptance does not legitimize the prohibited.
4
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical custom - for example, a community that practices riba-based financing - apply the maxim: the custom is void because it contradicts the explicit Quranic prohibition of riba.
The ruling holds regardless of how entrenched the custom is.
5
Note the exception
Understand that if the text is zanni (speculative in transmission or meaning) and the custom is widespread and consistent, the custom may specify the text (takhsis) according to some Hanafi authorities. However, qat'i texts (definitive) cannot be overridden.
This is the istithna recorded in the qawida panel.

Source Text

لا الشارع ونهيه لأنَّ الشارع يزن الأمور وينظر إلى نتائجها من جميع نواحيها من بعض النواحي دون بعض. فما نهى عنه بخصوصه يجب أن يُعتبر مضراً ولو أنه نافع لمئات أو فئات (ر: ف٧/٦٧).
وكل تشريع إنما يقوم على أساس تقييد حرية المكلفين في بعض ميادين العمل وإطلاقها في بعض، بحسب ما يرى الشارع ويقدر من وجوه المصلحة العامة. وقد تتفاوت حدود هذا الإطلاق والتقييد بين شريعة وأخرى. وهذا مقرَّر في النظريات القانونية اليوم أيضاً، فنصوص القوانين لا يغير حكمها العرف المخالف .
ونظير هذا نظر القوانين الوضعية اليوم إلى قضايا وأحكام يراها واضع القانون من النظام العام فيحجر حرية المكلفين عن كل اتفاق أو عرف على خلافها، ويعتبره باطلا (۱) .
٥/٧١ - ولذا جاءت الشريعة الإسلامية بالنهي عن كثير من الأعمال والعقود التي كانت متعارفة في الجاهلية بلا نكير فحرمت الغزو الداخلي واستباحة الناس الأموال والأعراض به وأقامت دولة ونظاماً أخلاقياً واجتماعياً وحقوقياً أخضعت له الجميع، مع أن الغزو الداخلي كان عرفاً مألوفاً في جاهلية العرب ولا يزال معتاداً لدى قبائل من البدو في بوادي بلادنا وغيرها.
وكذلك نهى النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن عقود كانت متعارفة بين العرب لانتفاء التراضي الحر فيها لما فيها من غرر ومشكلات. من نهيه عن البيع بالمنابذة والملامسة وإلقاء الحجر، وبيع الملاقيح والمضامين وبيع ضربة القانص والغائص (۱)، وكان كل ذلك معروفاً في الجاهلية، فنهى عنه النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام فأصبح في الإسلام ممنوعاً باطلاً. فلو عاود أهل بلد شيئاً منه وتعارفوه فلا عبرة لعرفهم.
ومثل ذلك استرقاق المدين الذي كان متعارفاً في جاهلية العرب وعند الرومانيين، فجاء الإسلام بمنعه وأوجب النظرة للمدين المعسر بنص القرآن الصريح في قوله تعالى: ﴿ وإن كان ذُو عُسْرَة فَنَظِرَةٌ إِلَى مَيْسَرَة ﴾ [سورة البقرة ٢٨٠/٢].
وكذلك عُرف أهل البر في نكاح الشغار باطل لا يقضى به (ر: الدرر، والدر المختار في كتاب النكاح).
ونكاح الشغار هذا هو أن يتفق شخصان فيزوج كل منهما الآخر قريبته
Chapter Nine: The Theory of Custom
No, the Lawgiver and His prohibition because the Lawgiver weighs matters and looks at their results from all aspects, not from some aspects without others. So what He specifically prohibited must be considered harmful even if it is beneficial to hundreds or categories (see: F 7/67).
Every legislation is based on restricting the freedom of the legally responsible in some fields of action and releasing it in others, according to what the Lawgiver sees and estimates from aspects of public interest. The limits of this release and restriction may vary between one law and another. This is also established in modern legal theories; the rulings of legal texts are not changed by contrary custom.
Analogous to this is the view of positive laws today on issues and rulings that the legislator considers to be of public order, thus restricting the freedom of the legally responsible from any agreement or custom contrary to them, and considering it void (1).
5/71 - Therefore, Islamic law came with prohibition of many practices and contracts that were customary in Jahiliyyah without denial; it prohibited internal raiding and the plundering of people's wealth and honor thereby, and established a state and a moral, social, and legal system to which all were subjected, although internal raiding was a familiar custom in the Arab Jahiliyyah and is still practiced by tribes of Bedouins in the deserts of our lands and others.
Likewise, the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited contracts that were customary among the Arabs due to the lack of free consent therein because of the gharar (uncertainty) and problems they contained. Among his prohibitions were: sale by munabadhah, mulamasah, throwing a stone, sale of malaqih and madamin, and sale by the strike of the hunter and diver (1); all that was known in Jahiliyyah, then the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited it, so it became in Islam forbidden and void. If the people of a town revert to something of it and adopt it as custom, their custom is not considered.
Similar to that is the enslavement of a debtor, which was customary in the Arab Jahiliyyah and among the Romans; Islam prohibited it and obligated respite for the insolvent debtor by the explicit Quranic text in His statement: "And if someone is in hardship, then let there be postponement until a time of ease" [Surah al-Baqarah 2:280].
Likewise, the custom of the people of the desert regarding shighar marriage is invalid and not to be ruled by (see: al-Durar, al-Durr al-Mukhtar in the Book of Marriage).
Shighar marriage is that two persons agree, each marrying off his relative to the other.
Source pages p. 849

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-ʿAam discusses a fundamental principle in the Hanafi theory of custom: a valid custom that contradicts an explicit legal text (nass) is not recognized. The author explains that the Lawgiver (Allah) evaluates actions holistically; if He specifically prohibits something, it is considered harmful even if it appears beneficial. Legislation inherently involves restricting freedom in some areas for public interest. Just as modern legal systems treat certain laws as public order and void any contrary agreement, Islamic law upholds its explicit texts over contrary customs. The author provides several historical examples: (1) internal raiding (al-ghazw al-dakhili) was a pre-Islamic Arab custom that Islam prohibited; (2) various invalid sales (munabadhah, mulamasah, throwing a stone, malaqih, madamin, hunter's strike, diver's strike) were prohibited by the Prophet due to uncertainty and lack of free consent; (3) enslavement of debtors was prohibited by the Quranic verse commanding respite for the insolvent; (4) shighar marriage (exchange marriage without mahr) was declared void. The key takeaway: if a prohibited practice re-emerges and becomes customary among people, that custom is given no legal weight in Islamic law. The Hanafi position is clear: custom cannot overrule a definitive text. The examples also illustrate that even widespread acceptance does not legitimize what is explicitly forbidden. The passage also notes that modern positive laws in Muslim countries may permit such practices, but from an Islamic legal perspective they remain invalid.

Key Terms
العرف (al-ʿurf): Custom or common practice that is consistent and accepted among people.
النص الخاص (al-nass al-khass): A specific legal text from Quran or Hadith that addresses a particular matter definitively.
الشغار (al-shighār): A marriage where two men give their female relatives to each other in marriage without mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi theory of custom as explained by al-Zarqa, what is the ruling if a town reverts to the pre-Islamic practice of shighar marriage?
A) The marriage is valid because it has become customary among them.
B) The marriage is invalid and not to be ruled by, regardless of custom.
C) The marriage is valid only if both parties agree to forgo the mahr.
D) The marriage is temporarily tolerated until a new custom emerges.

Key Takeaway
An explicit legal text from Quran or Sunnah overrides any contrary custom, no matter how widespread.

The General Rule: Custom Cannot Override a Specific Text, with the Exception of Customary Texts
Rule that custom cannot override a specific text, with an exception for custom-based texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a specific legislative text overrides any custom, and identify when a text is 'urfi, making its ruling subject to change with custom.

Core Idea
A specific text overrides custom, unless the text itself was built on a custom and reasoned by it.

This passage from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm by Mustafa al-Zarqa establishes a crucial principle for muftis: custom (urf) cannot override a specific text from the Quran or Sunnah. However, an important exception exists for texts that are inherently custom-based ('urfi). Understanding this distinction is essential for correct fatwa issuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific text
Determine if there is a clear Quranic verse or authentic hadith that directly governs the matter at hand. This is the nass khas.
If no specific text exists, custom may operate.
2
Assess the text's nature
Check whether the text was revealed based on a prevailing custom and is reasoned by it (nas 'urfi) or is an absolute legislative ruling not tied to custom.
Examples: the definition of ribawi goods by weight/measure is 'urfi; the prohibition of riba itself is not.
3
Apply the rule or exception
If the text is not 'urfi, enforce it regardless of any contrary custom. If it is 'urfi, then consider whether the custom has changed; if so, the ruling may change accordingly.
This requires careful ijtihad; jurists may differ on whether a text is 'urfi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وبيع ضربة القانص والغائص
، (۱)
