Liability of Usurper for Usufruct: Changing Ruling Due to Moral Decay
Example of fasad al-zaman causing change in ruling on ghasb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept of fasad al-zaman to justify a change in a fatwa and evaluate the scope of the later Hanafi ruling on usurper liability.

Core Idea
When moral decay weakens deterrence, Hanafi jurists may override qiyas to impose liability on usurpers for usufruct.

This passage from the chapter on custom ('urf) demonstrates how later Hanafi jurists used the principle of fasad al-zaman (corruption of the time) to modify the school's original ruling on a usurper's liability for usufruct. The original ruling based on qiyas held that usufruct is not property, so no compensation is due. But due to widespread aggression and weak religious deterrent, later jurists issued a fatwa imposing liability for equivalent rent on three vulnerable types of property. The author argues this can be generalized to all properties today, and notes that the other three schools always required compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original Hanafi ruling
State the original position based on qiyas: the usurper is not liable for the usufruct because manafi' (usufructs) are not considered property (mal mutaqawwim) in the original Hanafi view.
This is the 'al-asl al-qiyasi' referred to.
2
Recognize the cause for change
Identify the sabab: the jurists observed 'tajarrū al-nās ʿalā al-ghaṣb' (audacity of people toward usurpation) and 'ḍuʿf al-wāziʿ al-dīnī' (weakness of religious deterrent). This is fasad al-zaman.
This is the key principle driving the change.
3
Describe the later fatwa
State the new ruling: the usurper must pay ujrat al-mithl (equivalent rent) for the period of usurpation, but only if the property is waqf, orphan's, or prepared for exploitation (maddan lil-istighlal).
This is a limited departure from the original qiyas.
4
Analyze the author's extension
The author argues that the same cause (tazāyud fasād al-dhimam) justifies generalizing the liability to all properties, not just the three types.
This is an expansion based on continued moral decay.
5
Compare with the three Imams
Note that Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools always consider usufruct valuable and oblige compensation. The author finds their ijtihad 'awjah' (more sound).
This is a cross-madhhab evaluation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب التاسع : نظرية العرف
الإجارة، ولا عقد في الغصب
(۱)
ولكن المتأخرين من فقهاء المذهب الحنفي نظروا تجرؤ الناس على الغصب، وضعف الوازع الديني في نفوسهم، فأفتوا بتضمين الغاصب أجرة المثل عن منافع المغصوب إذا كان المغصوب مال وقف أو مال يتيم أو معداً للاستغلال على خلاف الأصل القياسي في المذهب، زجراً للناس عن العدوان الفساد الزمان وهذه الأموال الثلاثة مطمع لضعف الباعث الشخصي على حمايتها .
وعلى هذا استقرَّ العمل وجاءت المجلة (ر: م/ ٥٩٦/ وشرحها) واستناداً إلى العلة نفسها نستطيع أن نقول : إنَّ قواعد الاجتهاد الحنفي تتقبل مبدأ تضمين بدل منافع المغصوب مطلقاً في جميع الأموال، لا في هذه الأنواع الثلاثة فقط، الازدياد فساد الذمم وكثرة الطمع في أموال الغير، والتجاوز على الحقوق.
وهذا التعميم في تضمين المنافع توجبه النصوص القانونية لدينا اليوم،
وفيه المصلحة .
(۱) وقد ذهب الأئمة الثلاثة إلى عكس ما ذهب إليه الاجتهاد الحنفي، فاعتبروا المنافع متقومة في ذاتها كالأعيان وأوجبوا تضمين الغاصب أجرة المثل عن المال المغصوب مدة الغصب، سواء استوفى الغاصب منافعه أو عطلها.
وهذا الاجتهاد أوجه ،وأصلح، كما سنرى في الجزء الثالث :(ر: ف ٤/١١ - ٤/١٢).
Chapter Nine: The Theory of Custom. Ijarah, and there is no contract in ghasb. (1) But the later jurists of the Hanafi school observed the audacity of people toward ghasb and the weakness of religious deterrent in their souls, so they issued fatwa to hold the usurber liable for the equivalent rent for the usufruct of the usurped property if the usurped property is waqf property, orphan's property, or property prepared for exploitation, contrary to the analogical principle of the school, as a deterrent against aggression due to the corruption of time. These three types of property are tempting due to the weakness of personal motive to protect them. And upon this the practice settled, and the Majallah came (see Article 596 and its commentary). And based on the same cause, we can say that the rules of Hanafi ijtihad accept the principle of liability for the substitute of usufruct of usurped property absolutely in all properties, not only in these three types, due to the increase in corruption of consciences and the frequency of greed for others' properties and transgression against rights. And this generalization in liability for usufruct is required by our legal texts today, and in it is maslahah. (1) The three Imams went opposite to what Hanafi ijtihad went, considering usufructs as valuable in themselves like tangible assets, and obligated the usurper to pay the equivalent rent for the usurped property during the period of usurpation, whether the usurper utilized its usufruct or left it idle. And this ijtihad is more sound and more appropriate, as we will see in Part Three (see F 4/11-4/12).
Source pages p. 885

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on custom ('urf) and illustrates how Hanafi jurists modify rulings due to changing circumstances (fasad al-zaman). The original ruling (based on qiyas) held that a usurper is not liable for the usufruct of a usurped property because usufruct is not considered property in the original Hanafi view. However, later jurists observed widespread aggression and weak religious commitment. They issued a fatwa that the usurper must pay the equivalent rent (ujrat al-mithl) for the usufruct, but only for three specific types of property: waqf, orphan's property, and property prepared for rental exploitation. This was to deter injustice. The author notes that this principle can be extended to all properties due to persistent moral decay. He also cites the Majallah (Ottoman Civil Code) as having adopted this view. A footnote mentions that the three other Sunni imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) consider usufruct valuable and always require compensation, which the author deems more sound.

Key Terms
الغصب (al-ghaṣb): Usurpation: taking another's property without right and without khilaf (dispute).
منافع (manāfiʿ): Usufructs: the benefits or uses of a property.
فساد الزمان (fasād al-zamān): Corruption of the time: moral decay and widespread injustice in society.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the three types of property for which the later Hanafi fatwa initially imposed liability for usufruct?
A) Waqf, orphan's, and agricultural land
B) Waqf, orphan's, and property prepared for exploitation
C) Waqf, government property, and mosque property
D) Orphan's, inheritance, and charity

Key Takeaway
Later Hanafi jurists modified the ruling on usurper liability for usufruct based on fasad al-zaman, initially for three vulnerable property types, and this can be generalized when moral decay persists.

Change of Ruling Due to Fasad al-Zaman: The Wife's Duty to Follow Her Husband
Second example of fasad al-zaman affecting family law ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the change in the Hanafi ruling on the wife's duty to follow her husband due to corruption of time, and apply the principle of fasad al-zaman to modern fatwa instances.

Core Idea
A ruling changes when the moral and social reality changes — fasad al-zaman modifies the mufta bihi.

This passage from al-Zarqa's work illustrates a key principle in Hanafi fatwa methodology: when societal conditions become corrupt, a ruling can shift to prevent harm. Here, the original rule required a wife to follow her husband anywhere, but later jurists, observing widespread injustice, limited this duty to the wife's homeland. Understanding this evolution is essential for a mufti navigating between textual precedents and changing realities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Original Ruling
Find in the passage the original Hanafi position: the wife, upon receiving her prompt dower, must accompany her husband wherever he wishes.
The original ruling is based on the husband's authority and the wife's duty of obedience.
2
Observe the Change Trigger
Note the later jurists' observation: 'reversal of morals, prevalence of tyranny, husbands taking wives to distant lands without support and mistreating them.' This is the talil (ratio legis) for the change.
Fasad al-zaman is the cause; the illah is preventing harm (darar) to the wife.
3
State the Modified Ruling
The later fatwa: the wife is not compelled to follow her husband to a place unless it is her original homeland where the marriage contract took place. Receipt of prompt dower does not change this.
The condition is 'being in her homeland' — this limits the wife's obligation.
4
Analyze the Role of Prompt Dower
The original ruling made the wife's obligation conditional on receiving prompt dower. The later ruling removes this condition: even if she received it, she is still not forced to go to a non-homeland.
This shows that the later jurists prioritized preventing harm over contractual rights.
5
Reflect on Subsequent Legal Codes
The passage notes that the Ottoman Family Rights Law reverted to the original rule but gave the wife a right to seek judicial separation. The 1953 Syrian law required travel unless stipulated otherwise or the judge finds a hindrance.
This shows how later legislation balances original and later positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل (77) تغير الأحكام الاجتهادية بفساد الزمان
مهره
من
٤/٧٧ - ج - في أصل المذهب الحنفي أنَّ الزوجة إذا قَبَضَت معجل ها تلزم بمتابعة زوجها حيث شاء. ولكن المتأخرين لحظوا انقلاب الأخلاق وغلبة الجور، وأن كثيراً الرجال يسافرون بزوجاتهم إلى بلاد نائية ليس لهن فيها أهل ولا نصير، فيسيئون معاملتهن ويجورون عليهن فأفتى المتأخرون بأن المرأة، ولو قبضت معجل ،مهرها لا تجبر على متابعة زوجها إلى مكان إلا إذا كان وطناً لها، وقد جرى فيه عقد الزواج بينهما، وذلك لفساد الزمان وأخلاق الناس. وعلى هذا استقرت الفتوى والقضاء في المذهب (۱) .
ر) باب المهر في كتاب النكاح في الدرر ٣٤٧/١، وفي رد المحتار
.(٣٦٠/٢
(1) يلحظ هنا أن المادة /71/ من قانون حقوق العائلة العثماني» الذي كان نافذاً لدينا جاءت توجب على المرأة متابعة زوجها حيث شاء رجوعاً إلى أصل المذهب لأن الزوج أدرى بموطن رزقه.
والسبب في هذا الرجوع أن القانون المذكور قد فتح في المادة / 130/ منه للمرأة طريق الخلاص بطلب التفريق القضائي إن لم يطب لها المقام مع زوجها.
ثم جاءت المادة / 70 من قانون الأحوال الشخصية الصادر عام / 1953 ميلادية لدينا تقرر إجبار الزوجة على السفر مع زوجها إلا إذا اشترط في العقد غير ذلك، أو وجد مانعاً القاضي من السفر .
Chapter (77): Changing of Ijtihadi Rulings Due to Corruption of Time. (Reference) In the original Hanafi school, if a wife receives her prompt dower, she is obliged to follow her husband wherever he wishes. But later jurists observed the reversal of morals and prevalence of tyranny, and that many husbands travel with their wives to distant lands where they have no family or supporter, mistreating them and oppressing them. So later jurists issued a fatwa that a woman, even if she received her prompt dower, is not compelled to follow her husband to a place unless it is a homeland for her, and the marriage contract was concluded there, due to corruption of time and people's morals. And upon this the fatwa and judiciary settled in the school. (1) It is noted here that Article 71 of the Ottoman Family Rights Law, which was in effect here, obliged the wife to follow her husband wherever he wishes, returning to the original school because the husband knows best the location of his livelihood. The reason for this return is that the said law opened in Article 130 a way for the wife to seek judicial separation if she does not like living with her husband. Then Article 70 of the Personal Status Law issued in 1953 AD here decided to compel the wife to travel with her husband unless otherwise stipulated in the contract, or the judge finds a hindrance to travel.
Source pages p. 886

Commentary
This is another example of how fasad al-zaman changes rulings. The original Hanafi rule: a wife who receives her prompt dower (mahr mu'ajjal) must accompany her husband wherever he goes. Later jurists, seeing widespread injustice and husbands taking wives to remote places where they are mistreated, ruled that the wife cannot be forced to go to a place that is not her original homeland (where the marriage was contracted). This is based on the principle of preventing harm. The author then notes that later Ottoman and Syrian laws reverted to the original rule but provided a safety valve: the wife can request judicial separation if she is uncomfortable. This shows that later lawmakers considered both original and later positions.

Key Terms
المهر المعجل (al-mahr al-muʿajjal): Prompt dower: portion of mahr paid at the time of marriage.
فساد الزمان (fasād al-zamān): Corruption of the age; the decline in moral and social conditions that justifies a change in ruling.
متابعة الزوج (mutābaʿat al-zawj): The wife's duty to accompany her husband to his place of residence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi fatwa, under what condition is a wife not compelled to follow her husband?
A) If she did not receive her prompt dower
B) If the destination is not her homeland where the marriage was contracted
C) If the husband is oppressive
D) If she has no children

Key Takeaway
A ruling in the Hanafi school can change due to corruption of time (fasad al-zaman), as seen in the wife's duty to follow her husband, which was modified to prevent harm.

The Prohibition of Judging by Personal Knowledge Due to Corruption
Third example: prohibition due to corruption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school changed the ruling on a judge using personal knowledge and apply the principle of taghayyur al-ahkam bi-taghayyur al-azman.

Core Idea
A ruling may change when the maqsad is defeated by widespread corruption.

This passage illustrates the Hanafi legal principle that rulings can change when the circumstances that justified them no longer hold. Originally, judges could rely on their personal knowledge, but as corruption spread among judges, the later jurists prohibited this to prevent injustice. Understanding this shift is crucial for muftis who must apply the school's rulings in changing contexts.

Guided Path
1
State the original ruling
Identify the original Hanafi position: a judge may judge by his personal knowledge of the facts, as practiced by Umar ibn al-Khattab.
This was based on trust in the judge's integrity.
2
Identify the cause (sabab) of change
Find the reason cited in the text: judges became corrupt, took bribes, and were appointed based on sycophancy rather than integrity.
The sabab is fasad al-zaman (corruption of the times).
3
Explain the new ruling
State the later fatwa: a judge cannot rely on personal knowledge; all judgments must be based on evidence presented in court.
Even if the judge personally witnessed the event, he must not use that knowledge.
4
Analyze the rationale (ta'lil)
Explain why the change was made: to prevent corrupt judges from falsely claiming knowledge and favoring one party, thereby preventing much falsehood.
The maqsad (objective) is to uphold justice and prevent abuse.
5
Apply the principle
Generalize: when the effective cause (illah) for a ruling is corrupted, the ruling may be changed to protect the maqsad.
This is an application of the maxim 'al-hukm yaduru ma'a illatihi wujudan wa 'adaman'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٧٧ ٥ ـ د ـ في أصل المذهب الحنفي وغيره أن القاضي يقضي بعلمه الشخصي في الحوادث أي إنَّ علمه بالوقائع المتنازع فيها يصلح مستنداً لقضائه ويغني المدَّعي عن إثبات مُدَّعَاه بالبينة، فيكون علم القاضي بواقع الحال هو البينة. وفي ذلك أقضية مأثورة عن عمر وغيره. ولكن لوحظ فيما بعد أنّ القضاة قد غلب عليهم الفساد والسوء وأخذ الرّشا، ولم يعد يختار للقضاء الأوفر ثقةً وعفةً وكفاية، بل الأكثر تَزَلُّفاً إلى الولاة، وسعياً في استرضائهم وإلحافاً في طلب التوظيف.
لذلك أفتى المتأخرون بأنه لا يصح أن يقضي القاضي بعلمه الشخصي في الوقائع، بل لا بد أن يستند قضاؤه إلى البينات المثبتة في مجلس القضاء. حتى لو شاهد القاضي بنفسه عقداً أو قرضاً أو واقعة ما بين اثنين خارج مجلس القضاء، ثم ادعى بها أحدهما وجَحَدها الآخر، فليس للقاضي أن يقضي للمدعي بلا بينة؛ إذ لو سَاغَ ذلك بعدما فَسَدت ذمم كثير من القضاة لزعموا العلم بالوقائع زوراً وميلاً مع الأقوى وسيلة من الخصمين. فهذا المنع، وإن أضاع بعض الحقوق لفقدان الإثبات، يدفع باطلاً كثيراً.
77 5 - D: In the original Hanafi school and others, a judge may judge by his personal knowledge in incidents, meaning his knowledge of the disputed facts is a valid basis for his judgment and relieves the plaintiff from proving his claim with evidence; thus the judge's knowledge of the reality is the evidence. There are rulings transmitted from Umar and others regarding this. But later it was observed that judges were overcome by corruption and evil and taking bribes, and the most trustworthy and chaste and competent were no longer chosen for judgeship, but rather those who grovel to the rulers, seek to appease them, and are insistent in seeking employment. Therefore, the later jurists issued a fatwa that it is not valid for a judge to judge by his personal knowledge in incidents; rather, his judgment must be based on evidence proven in the courtroom. Even if the judge himself witnessed a contract, a loan, or an incident between two people outside the courtroom, and then one of them claims it and the other denies it, the judge cannot rule for the plaintiff without evidence. Because if that were permissible after the corruption of many judges' consciences, they would falsely claim knowledge of incidents, biasing toward the stronger party. This prohibition, even though it may cause loss of some rights due to lack of evidence, prevents much falsehood.
Source pages p. 886

Commentary
This is the third example of how fasad al-zaman changes legal rulings. Originally, judges were allowed to use their personal knowledge of a case as evidence, based on the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab and others. However, later jurors saw that judges became corrupt, accepting bribes, and appointments were based on sycophancy rather than integrity. The potential for abuse became too great. Therefore, later Hanafi jurists ruled that a judge cannot rely on his personal knowledge; all judgments must be based on evidence presented in court. Even if the judge personally witnessed the event, he must not use that knowledge. The reason is to prevent corrupt judges from falsely claiming knowledge to favor one party. Thus, despite possibly losing some legitimate claims, the system becomes more just overall.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, specifically testimony of witnesses or documentary proof in court.
علم القاضي الشخصي (ilm al-qadi al-shakhsi): The personal knowledge of the judge about the facts of a case outside the courtroom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the primary reason for the later Hanafi fatwa prohibiting a judge from judging by personal knowledge?
A) It contradicts the Quran
B) Judges became corrupt and took bribes
C) Caliph Umar forbade it
D) It confused the litigants

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school shows that rulings can change to preserve justice when the underlying conditions causing the original ruling are corrupted.

12 min
Change of Ijtihadi Rulings Due to Corruption of Time
Chapter on custom with four examples of later Hanafi modifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qawida 'Tughayyur al-ahkam al-ijtihadiyya bi fasad al-zaman' and apply it to the four cases of judge's personal knowledge in administrative matters, wages for obligatory religious duties, acceptance of witnesses with relative uprightness, and moon sighting testimony, identifying the scope and limits of the principle.

Core Idea
Ijtihadi rulings adapt to changing custom; fixed texts remain unchanged.

This passage from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm illustrates how the later Hanafi jurists (al-muta'akhkhirun) applied the principle that ijtihadi rulings can change with the corruption of time. They observed declining religious commitment and practical necessities, and modified earlier rulings to preserve justice and religious institutions—without abandoning the school's foundational texts. Understanding this principle is essential for muftis who must weigh custom and necessity against established doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle and its scope
Locate the heading 'الفصل (۷۷) تغير الأحكام الاجتهادية بفساد الزمان' and note that it asserts a general rule. Understand that this change applies only to rulings based on ijtihad and custom, not to definitive texts (nusus qat'iyya).
The principle is anchored in the broader theory of custom ('urf).
2
Analyze the first application: judge's personal knowledge in administrative matters
The original rule prohibits a judge from basing a judgment on his private knowledge. However, the later jurists allowed him to act on his knowledge in non-judicial hisbah and administrative matters, such as separating a divorced couple or safeguarding usurped property.
This shows a relaxation of procedural strictness to prevent harm.
3
Analyze the second application: wages for obligatory religious duties
The original Hanafi position forbids taking wages for obligatory acts like leading prayer or teaching Qur'an. Due to declining motivation and cessation of state funding, the later jurists permitted wages to ensure continuity of these duties.
This was a major shift; the madhhab_dispute_map details the cross-school disagreement.
4
Analyze the third and fourth applications: witnesses and moon sighting
For testimony, complete uprightness ('adalah) is normally required. Scarcity of upright witnesses led to accepting 'the best available' (al-amthal fa al-amthal). For moon sighting, the original requirement of a large crowd in clear sky was relaxed to two trustworthy witnesses due to public apathy in seeking the crescent.
Both examples involve lowering evidentiary standards to prevent loss of rights and to facilitate religious practice.
5
Extract the limitation and related maxims
Note the istithna': only ijtihadi rulings change, not those based on definitive texts. Connect the qawida to related maxims like 'المشقة تجلب التيسير' (hardship brings ease) and 'الضرر يزال' (harm must be removed).
This ties the principle into the broader Hanafi legal philosophy.

من المبادىء المقررة في أصل المذهب أن العمل الواجب على شخص شرعاً لا يصح استئجاره فيه ولا يجوز له أخذ أجرة عليه .

الفصل (۷۷) تغير الأحكام الاجتهادية بفساد الزمان
لذلك أفتى المتأخرون بجواز أخذ الأجور عليها حرصاً على تعليم القرآن ونشر العلم وإقامة الشعائر الدينية بين الناس.
۷/۷۷ - و - إنَّ الشهود الذين يُقضى بشهادتهم في الحوادث يجب أن يكونوا عدولاً، أي ثقات وهم المحافظون على الواجبات الدينية، المعروفون بالصدق والأمانة. وإن عدالة الشهود شريطة اشترطها القرآن لقبول شهادتهم، وأيَّدتها السنة وأجمع عليها فقهاء الإسلام.
غير أنَّ المتأخرين من فقهائنا لحظوا نُذرة العدالة الكاملة التي فسرت بها النصوص، لفسادِ الزمن وضعف الذمم وفتور الحس الديني الوازع . فإذا تطلب القضاة دائماً نِصَابَ العدالة الشرعية في الشهود ضاعت الحقوق لامتناع الإثبات. فلذا أفتوا بقبول شهادة الأمثل فالأمثل من القوم حيث تَقِلُ العدالة الكاملة .
ومعنى الأمثل فالأمثل : الأحسن فالأحسن حالاً بين الموجودين، ولو كان في ذاته غير كامل العدالة بحدها الشرعي أي أنهم تنازلوا عن اشتراط العدالة المطلقة إلى العدالة النسبية . ر : معين «الحكام القسم الثاني، الباب السماء علة ٢٢ ص/ ١٤٥).
۸/۷۷ - ز - وكذلك أفتى المتأخرون في إثبات الأهلة لصيام رمضان وللعيدين بقبول رؤية شخصين، ولو لم يكن في تمنع الرؤيا من غيم أو ضباب أو غبار، بعد أن كان في أصل المذهب الحنفي لا يثبت إهلال الهلال عند صفاء السماء إلا برؤية جمع عظيم، لأن معظم الناس يلتمسون الرؤية. فانفراد اثنين بادعاء الرؤية مظنَّة الغَلَط أو الشبهة.
وقد عَلَّل المتأخرون قبول رؤية الاثنين بقعود همم الناس عن التماس رؤية الهلال فلم تبق رؤية اثنين منهم مَظنَّة الغلط إذا لم يكن في شهادتهما شبهة أو تهمة تدعو إلى الشك والريبة ( ر ) البحر الرائق لابن نجيم، ورسالة العرف والعادة للأستاذ أبي سنة ص/ ١١١ - ١١٢).

Chapter Nine: Theory of Custom. And thus the practice of the later scholars settled upon the non-enforcement of the judge's ruling based on his personal knowledge. (1): But the judge may rely on his knowledge in non-judicial matters of hisbah and precautionary administrative measures, such as if he knows of the irrevocable divorce of a woman while cohabitation continues between her and her husband, or knows of usurpation of property, then he may separate the man and his divorced wife, and place the usurped property with a trustee until proof is established. 6/77 (2) Among the established principles in the fundamental [doctrine] of the school is that an act that is obligatory upon a person by law cannot be hired out, and he is not permitted to take a wage for it. And on this basis, if a usurper refuses to return the usurped property to its place of usurpation except for a fee, and the person from whom it was usurped pays it to him, the usurper does not deserve it; rather it is taken back from him. Even if a wife refuses to perform the work obligatory upon her religiously within the house, and the husband hires her for it, she does not deserve the wage. Among the branches of this juristic principle is that performing acts of worship and obligatory religious works, such as leading prayer, delivering the Friday sermon, teaching the Qur'an and sacred knowledge, it is not permissible to take a wage for them in the fundamental doctrine of the school; rather the capable one should do it for free because it is a religious duty. See: al-Bada'i', conditions of the subject matter in hire, 4/191-192. However, the later jurists of the school noticed the decline of aspirations regarding these duties and the cessation of stipends from the treasury for scholars, which compelled them to seek income, so much so that performing these duties became unguaranteed except with payment. (1) See: on the meaning of hisbah matters, what preceded f 1/13 footnote. Refer to: al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Radd al-Muhtar 4/345 and 355; al-Ashbah of Ibn Nujaym, the second art at the end of the Book of Judicial Sentencing; and Jami' al-Fusulayn vol. 1, end of first chapter p. 26, and middle of chapter ten p. 133 Azhari Press edition. 948 Chapter (77): Change of Ijtihadi Rulings Due to Corruption of Time. Therefore the later jurists gave fatwa permitting taking wages for them, out of concern for teaching the Qur'an, spreading knowledge, and establishing religious rites among the people. 7/77 - And: The witnesses who are accepted in adjudication of incidents must be upright ('udul), i.e., trustworthy, those who adhere to religious duties, known for truthfulness and honesty. Indeed, the uprightness of witnesses is a condition stipulated by the Qur'an for accepting their testimony, and the Sunnah affirmed it, and the jurists of Islam agreed upon it. However, the later jurists among us observed the scarcity of complete uprightness as interpreted by the texts, due to corruption of time, weakness of consciences, and lethargy of deterrent religious sentiment. If judges always required the level of legal uprightness in witnesses, rights would be lost due to impossibility of proof. Hence they gave fatwa accepting the testimony of the 'the best, then the best' among the people when complete uprightness is rare. And the meaning of 'the best, then the best' is the better, then the better in condition among those present, even if in itself it is not completely upright by its legal limit; i.e., they lowered the requirement from absolute uprightness to relative uprightness. See: Mu'in al-Hukkam, section two, chapter 22 p. 145. 8/77 - Z: And similarly, the later jurists gave fatwa regarding proof of the crescents for fasting Ramadan and for the two Eid festivals, accepting the sighting of two persons, even if there is no cloud, mist, or dust preventing sighting, whereas in the original doctrine of the Hanafi school the crescent is not established at a clear sky except by the sighting of a large multitude, because most people seek the sighting; the exclusive claim of two to sighting is a likely source of error or doubt. And the later jurists justified accepting the sighting of two by the decline of people's aspirations in seeking the crescent, so the sighting of two of them is no longer a likely source of error if there is no doubt or suspicion in their testimony that calls for uncertainty (see: al-Bahr al-Ra'iq of Ibn Nujaym, and Risalah al-'Urf wa al-'Adah by Professor Abu Sinnah pp. 111-112). 949

Commentary
This passage is from the section on the theory of custom ('urf) in al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm. The author, Mustafa al-Zarqa, is discussing the methodology of the later Hanafi jurists (al-muta'akhkhirin) in adapting rulings to the corruption of time (fasad al-zaman). He presents three key applications of the principle that ijtihadi rulings can change when circumstances deteriorate. First, he mentions the established rule that a judge cannot enforce a judgment based on his personal knowledge; but later jurists allowed him to act on his knowledge in non-judicial administrative or hisbah matters (e.g., separating a divorced couple living together or safeguarding usurped property). Second, the original principle that one cannot take wages for performing obligatory acts (like prayer leadership, teaching Qur'an) is modified: later jurists permitted taking wages due to people's negligence and the drying up of state funding, to preserve religious duties. Third, the strict requirement of complete 'adalah (uprightness) in witnesses was relaxed: since perfect witnesses are rare, the later jurists accepted the 'best available' (amthal fa-amthal), i.e., relative uprightness. Fourth, the rule for moon sighting: originally, a clear sky required a large crowd for testimony; later, due to decreased public interest, they accepted two witnesses if no suspicion exists. These examples illustrate how the mufti must consider changing customs and conditions, a core theme of rasm al-mufti. The passage reflects the Hanafi commitment to practical jurisprudence (fiqh al-waqi') without abandoning foundational texts.

Key Terms
المتأخرون (al-muta'akhkhirun): Later Hanafi jurists who modified earlier rulings in response to changing conditions, particularly from the 6th century AH onward.
فساد الزمان (fasad al-zaman): The corruption or moral decay of the age, leading to decline in religious commitment and justice.
الأمثل فالأمثل (al-amthal fa al-amthal): Selecting the relatively best candidate when complete uprightness is unavailable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On what basis did the later Hanafi jurists permit taking wages for teaching the Qur'an, contrary to the original school position?
A) They found a verse in the Qur'an allowing it.
B) They considered it a valid hire (ijarah) from the beginning.
C) They observed the decline of people's motivation and cessation of state funding, necessitating payment to preserve religious duties.
D) They ruled that obligatory acts are always hireable.

Key Takeaway
Ijtihadi rulings can change with the corruption of time, provided the change is based on necessity and does not contradict definitive texts.
